Date:    Tue, 30 Mar 1993 8:36:23 -0800 (PST)
From: LAFORCE@XENON.ARC.NASA.GOV
Subject: GGR autox/TT rules

Note to everyone on the Porschephiles mailing list:

Here are the new auto-x time-trial rules that Golden Gate 
Region (and, most likely, the rest of Zone 7) will be using
in 1994.

I hope they are of use to someone.

- --Soren            laforce@xenon.arc.nasa.gov

By the way, much as I'd like to, I can't take any credit for
the proposal.  The "gang of seven" is listed below.

***************************************************************


                PORSCHE

GGR AUTOCROSS AND TIME TRIAL RULES, 1994

                Revised 2Mar93
Zone 7 Drivers:

You are now holding Evolution '94, the rules by
which GGR will run our Time Trials and
Autocrosses, beginning next year.  These rules have
evolved over the last year.  A team of seven, Henry
Watts, Gary Dorighi, Bud Behrens, Dave Blanchard,
Tom Poole, Ken Mack and myself worked for over
six months to put the basic proposal together.  We
then asked for input from the racing membership at
Time Trials and Autocrosses.  We received a fantastic
amount of input, and these rules reflect the breadth
and depth of knowledge of the members of the club. 
I would like to thank the team of seven as well as all
of you who took the time to study the proposal and
then write or called us with your suggestions.  I
believe we have an incredibly solid foundation to
take us into the racing future.

The Evolution '94 team and the 1993 Driver's Events
Committee met on February 23 to put the final
touches on the rules proposal.  Evolution '94 will be
used as the 1994 rules after going through the usual
change process this year.  The schedule for that
process is:

          June 15: Deadline to send my your rules change
                proposals

          August Nugget: Change proposals printed

          August 17: Open meeting for comments on the
                proposed changes (tentative)

          August 31: Rules finalized by the Driver's Events
                Committee

          October Nugget: Approved revisions printed
          October 1: New rule books printed



/s/  Kirk Doberenz, 1993 Competition Director



Section 2.8(j) is added to the current rulebook, section 3.2(e) is
deleted, section 3.2T is replaced with the section 3.2T below, all of
section 4 is replaced, Appendix B is renamed to Appendix F.  All other
sections of the current rules are unaffected.


2.8 PROTESTS AND APPEALS
      (j): Camber Protests:  Protests involving allowable camber that result
           in the protestee being found to be in violation of camber limits
           by less than .25x shall be held in abeyance until the next event,
           at which time the car will be reinspected.  If the car is found to
           be in complete compliance at this second event, the original
           protest will be dropped.  If the car is not in complete compliance
           at the second event, the original protest will be upheld for that
           first event, and the car will be disqualified for both events.

           If, at the second event, the car is entered in a category that
           permits the camber settings measured at the first event, the car
           will, of course, be allowed to run in the second event, but will be
           disqualified for the event at which the protest was lodged.


3.2 SAFETY - AUTOMOBILES
      (e) [delete this section in the current rules]

3.2T  Time Trials
      (a) Roll Bars:  Roll bars (or cages) are recommended in all cars.

           Roll bars are required in all open cars.  914s and Targas are not
           open cars.

           Roll bars or cages are required non-open cars except in Stock and
           Improved Categories and except for student or provisional drivers
           in Production Category.

           Approved roll bars are defined in Appendix D.

      (b) Roll Cages:  Full roll cages are permitted, but must conform to
           the roll cage definition in Appendix D.

      (c) Fire Extinguishers:  Fire extinguishers are required for all cars and
           must be easily accessible to the driver in his seated position. 
           Minimum requirement is a 5 BC rating with a gauge.

      (d) Windows:  Passenger and driver's side windows must be down
           at all times.

      (e) Tire Rating:  All tires must have an HR or higher rating.



4.0 AUTOMOBILES
      (a) Purpose:  These rules are structured to inform participants what
           modifications are allowed.   This section defines the eligibility
           requirements, the allowable modifications and the car
           classifications for the different categories of automobiles listed
           below.  Refer to the specific section for definition of that
           category.  Also see Appendicies A, B and C.

      (b) The Categories & Reasons for them: 

                 Stock Category (compete in a daily driver)                4.1
                 Improved Category (low-cost, reversible changes)          4.2
                 Production Category (maximum performance without          
                        major engine/transmission work)                    4.3
                 Super-Production Category (Production + one step)         4.4

                 Prodified Category (budget racing for 914s)               4.5
                 Street Modified Category (fun w/ minimal restrictions)    4.6
                 Modified Category (maximum performance)                   4.7
                 Exhibition Category (avoid classes altogether)            4.8


      (c) The Classes:  See Appendicies A and B for the Classes for all cars.

           Additionally, Special classes, to be designated S1, S2, etc., can
           be created by any three or more competitors who decide to run
           against each other.  The competitors must petition the
           chairperson of the series (autocross or time trial) before the end
           of the first event of the season.  Year-end trophies shall be
           awarded only if at least three competitors participate in enough
           events to earn an award.

      (d) Specificity:  The rules only define what is permitted.  If the
           modification is not specifically allowed by the rules, it is not
           permitted. 

      (e) Update/Backdate:  Any car may be entered as a different car
           than originally manufactured, provided it matches the car as
           which it is being run in all performance-related specifics.  These
           include (but are not limited to) weight, weight distribution
           (front/rear and side-to-side), center-of-gravity height, gearing,
           power, torque, suspension, and airflow.

           In addition to normal update/backdate, this provides a potential
           path for limited edition cars and European-specification cars to
           compete in some categories, provided they can be legitimately
           configured.

      (f) U.S. Delivered Cars:  Within the Stock, Improved, Production and
           Super-Production Categories, cars are defined as U.S. model
           specification Porsches that were normally delivered to the U.S.
           public for general road use through the manufacturer's
           authorized sales outlet.

           Unless otherwise specified, European cars and parts are not
           considered stock.  Owners of European-specification cars may run
           these cars in any class that would allow, as legal modifications,
           all of the relevant differences between the U.S model and the
           European model of that car.  For example, if the only differences
           between the European and U.S models were in the chip and in a
           compression ratio difference of less than .5 points, that car could
           run in the production class.  Cars with larger motors than were
           delivered in the U.S. would certainly have to move to at least the
           Super-Production Category.

      (g) Limited-Edition Cars:  Special Porsches, produced in quantities of
           less than 400, are not considered identical to the model on which
           they are based.  

           If not covered in the list below, such cars must be modified to
           fully conform to the specifications of a class, or they may run in
           the Super Street Category, (provided they came from the factory
           with a proper interior - if not they run in the Modified Category).

           The 924S SE may not compete in the Stock or Improved
                 Categories, due to the 951 front struts.
           The '75 911 Carrera and the 911 Weissach (SC) may not time trial
                 in the Stock or Improved Categories (due to the rear wing)
                 unless they elect to run against the stock or improved 911 3.2
                 Carrera, which they may do, or they remove the wing and
                 substitute a standard engine cover.
           The RS America runs as a C2.  The car is only slightly lighter than
                 the C2, even if the airconditioning option is not selected; 
                 most cars coming to America have air conditioning.  Further,
                 the suspension modifications are all available as a sport
                 suspension package on the C2
           Other models may be restricted as needed by the Drivers Events
           Committee.

      (h) Similar Equipment in a Class:  Unless specifically prohibited, cars
           may run with the same performance-related equipment (wheels,
           brakes, wings, etc.) allowed any competitor in the same class. 
           This does not override the tire/wheel specifications in Appendix
           A.

      (i) Noise:  Site Restrictions may require effective noise mufflers. 
           Students are required to run effective mufflers to allow
           instruction.

      (j) Fuel:  Any gasoline fuel is permitted.  Additives (non-oxygen
           bearing) may be used as long as they do not constitute more
           than 10% of the fuel.

      (k) Aerodynamic Devices:  Devices which articulate or adjust when
           the car is in motion are prohibited, except for the normal devices
           on the C2s and C4s.

      (l) 14" Wheels:  Some models of Porsches (911E, late 912, 924,
           etc.) were originally equipped with 14" wheels.  Owners of such
           cars may legitimately argue that these cars should be permitted
           to run such wheels.  However, unless some other adjustment is
           made, such cars may have a substantial overall gearing
           advantage, especially during autocrossing.  Therefore, any car
           that was originally equipped with 14" wheels may run such
           wheels, but must, if competing in Stock, Improved or Production
           Categories, run tires that are one step larger in aspect ratio (60
           series instead of 50 series, for example) than what is permitted in
           Appendix A.



4.1 STOCK CATEGORY 
      (a) Purpose:  The purpose of the Stock Category is to provide for
           cars which are driven on a daily basis, on normal street tires, and
           owned by people who do not wish to modify their car, buy extra
           sets of wheels, or spend time changing tires.  For many
           competitors this will be a logical starting category.

           Most of the modifications allowed in the Stock Category are not
           performance-enhancing changes.  Other modifications are
           allowed because some normal, stock cars were delivered that
           way, and it makes no sense to either prevent such cars from
           running or to allow such drivers to have an unfair competitive
           advantage over cars that did not have such features.  Some
           permitted modifications support the proper rebuild of older
           engines. 

      (b) Non-Performance Modifications:  Any modification that is clearly
           not related to performance is permitted.  Such modifications must
           have no significant enhancing effect on weight, weight
           distribution (front/rear and side-to-side), center-of-gravity height,
           gearing, power, torque, suspension, or airflow.

      (c) Adjustments:  Except as noted, any modification for the sole
           purpose of facilitating adjustment of the car or the motor (such
           as modified valve adjusters) are permitted.  Adjustable spring
           plates are not covered by this provision (and therefore not
           allowed in the Stock Category) as they introduce plastic bushing
           material.  914 adjustable rear spring perches are permitted, as
           long as the original spring is used.

      (d) Cooling:  Any oil-, water-, or air-cooling change which allows the
           engine to run cooler is permitted, unless otherwise prohibited. 
           The 914 plastic engine cover water tray may be removed.  Such
           changes tend to extend engine life and should be encouraged.

      (e) Seats:  Aftermarket seats may be substituted for the stock seats. 
           Such seats must have an adjustment for seatback angle, except in
           914s.  This allows the replacement of worn seats without
           excessive lightening of the car.

      (f) Fuel Pump:  Any fuel pump may be used.  Fuel pumps should
           not be a problem.  If, in a specific case, the fuel pump is a
           limiting factor, the driver should be allowed to correct the
           problem.

      (g) Balancing:  The motor may be balanced.  Note that this is not
           necessarily a recommended procedure.  Most Porsche engines are
           built so precisely that they will not achieve any noticeable
           performance increase through balancing.

      (h) Lubrication System:   Modifications to the lubrication system
           designed to provide a constant source of engine lubrication are
           permitted, including oil traps, extended sumps and push rod
           tubes, baffling and pressurized systems.  Such changes tend to
           extend engine life and should be encouraged.

      (i) Motor Re-builds:  To allow for normal rebuilds, the motor may
           be overbored to a maximum of .5mm.  Note: to remain in the
           Stock or Improved Category, any motor which is rebuilt must
           retain the stock compression ratio.  If any procedures (such as
           truing the heads) change the compression ratio, cylinder spacers
           or other parts and/or techniques must be used to bring the motor
           back to stock compression ratio.

      (j) Chain Tensioner:  Any chain tensioner or chain guard is
           permitted.

      (k) Popoff Valve:  A spring-loaded popoff valve may be used with
           any 911 CIS fuel injection system.  This does not change the
           performance of the engine, but may prevent major problems.

      (l) Mufflers & Heat Exchangers:  Any muffler which is functionally
           equivalent to the stock muffler may be used.  This allows owner
           to replace wornout mufflers with reasonable-cost options, but
           does not allow performance-enhancing mufflers in the stock
           category.

      (m) Short-Shift Kits:  Any short-shift kit may be used.  Short-shift
           kits are a valid factory option, though not common on the early
           cars.  Further, the short-shift kit is not necessarily a performance-
           enhancing option.

      (n) Limited-Slip Differentials:  Cars other than 356s, 914s, 914-6s,
           924s and 912s and pre-1978 911s may use any limited slip
           differential.  This is to take into account that such differentials
           are somewhat common on the other cars.  However, limited-slip
           differentials are not common on the cars listed, and allowing
           them in the stock class would create an undue hardship on the
           majority of the drivers of these cars, who might feel that they
           would have to install such a device to be competitive.  The cars in
           this list may install limited slip differentials in the Production
           Category

      (o) Fenders:  Fenders may be rolled.  Flared fenders are permissible,
           but do not change the allowable wheel/tire sizes or the maximum
           offsets permitted.  This allows competitors to drive with larger
           tires/wheels on the street, if they desire.  As long as valid
           tire/wheel combinations are specified for competition, there is no
           competitive advantage to flares or rolling.

      (p) Interior Options:  Any steering wheel may be used, as long as a
           factory airbag device is not removed when the wheel is changed. 
           Floormats and trunk mats may be removed.  Seatbacks in the
           rear passenger compartment may be removed.  The seatbacks
           are useless if a rollbar is installed, and many people prefer to
           have them out anyway.

      (q) Shocks:  Any steel-bodied, singly adjustable (damping or
           rebound, but not both) shock absorber may be used.  The shock
           must be mounted right-side-up.  Thus, people may replace worn
           with any reasonable street shock.

      (r) 914 Chassis Stiffening:  914s are permitted a factory-type rear
           chassis stiffening set.  Alternate bracing for the 914 'inner'
           suspension mount may be used.  Such alternate bracing shall not
           be attached to the roll bar or the roll cage attachement points. 
           Bolted flanges may be used to hold a tubing (1" square) 'X
           brace' to the body.  This is to allow the motor to be removed. 
           Such bracing shall fall within the limits indicated by the sketch
           given in Appendix D, 914 Bracing.  Such stiffening is allowed in
           the Stock Category to solve problems with worn/deteriorated
           chassis.  Such stiffening should not be of noticeable help to 914s
           that are in good condition and are restricted to stock suspension
           and hard-compound street tires.

      (s) Alignment Settings:  Any setting may be used, except for
           camber.  Camber is the single most important suspension setting
           for competition.  Camber settings are limited to 1x at the front
           of rear- or mid-engined cars, 1.5x at the rear of rear- or mid-
           engined cars, 1.5x at the front of front-engined cars and 1x at
           the rear of front-engined cars.  Camber measurements shall be
           the average of the readings from both sides of the car, with the
           driver seated in the driver seat.  This is to compensate for the
           lack of a known perfectly level surface when measuring camber in
           the field.  Keeping camber setting reasonable allows the car to
           be driven on the street without excessive tire wear on the inside
           edge.  

      (t) 911E Air Suspension:  911E-style air suspension may be replaced
           with the standard 911 torsion bar suspension.  This change is
           recommended.

      (u) Spare Tire:  The spare tire may be removed.

      (v) Tire Types:  Tire must show a wear rating of at least 120. 
           Sticky-compound or R-compound competition tires are not
           permitted.  The Drivers Events Committee may designate any tire
           as a sticky-compound competition tire.  Recapped tires are not
           permitted.  The wear-rating limitation helps restrict the Stock
           Category to cars that are normally driven on the street by people
           who do not want to spend time or money on extra wheels or
           changing tires.

      (w) Tire Wear:  All tires must have a DOT approved tread pattern. 
           At anytime during the event, tires must have at least 1/32" tread
           remaining in any two adjacent grooves at any location on the
           tire.  The measurement of tread depth shall not be made where
           tie bars, bumps or fillets are located.

      (x) Tire & Wheel Sizes:  Appendix A shows the allowable sizes for
           tires and wheels.  In the Stock Category, the allowable size is the
           base number.  The '+' number indicates the amount of increase
           available in other categories.

      (y) Brake Pads, Lines, Dustcovers:  Any brake pad may be used. 
           Any brake line with performance at least equal to original
           equipment may be used.  Dust covers may be removed.  The
           17mm and 19mm master cylinders may be used interchangeably. 
           Brake pads should be whatever the owner wants.  Upgrading the
           brake lines should be permitted in the interests of safety.

      (z) Air-conditioning:  Air-conditioning may be removed.  This is a
           valid delete-option on most models of Porsches.

      (aa) Removable Tops:  Removable tops may be removed; sunroofs
           may be open.  No reason to run in a closed car on a nice day.

      (bb) 356 Air Cleaners:  356s may upgrade the old, wire-mesh
           aircleaners to any aircleaner element.

      (cc) Mirrors:  Any interior and/or exterior mirrors may be used.

      (dd) Cam Timing:  Any cam timing may be used.



4.2 IMPROVED CATEGORY
      (a) Purpose:  The Improved Category provides competition
           opportunity for people who prefer to run on the stickier tires
           available, and who wish to make only relatively inexpensive and
           reversible changes to their Porsches.

           Most of the modifications permitted in the Improved Category
           (but not permitted in the Stock Category) are relatively
           inexpensive and reversable.  They tend not to interfere in the use
           of the car as a daily driver, as long as the owner doesn't mind
           the car being a bit taut.  Such changes are not permitted in Stock
           because they tend to violate the notion that a normal daily driver
           can be driven to the track and run as is.

      (b) All of the modifications permitted in the Stock Category are
           permitted.

      (c) Sway Bars:  Alternate sway bars may be used, including
           adjustable sway bars, except that, in keeping with the objective
           of reversibility, no part of the original car may be cut (914s may
           cut the sheet metal necessary, as this is done for all 914 sway-bar
           installations).  This effectively means that late models 911s
           running in the Improved Category may not switch to adjustable
           front sway bars.

      (d) Track Increase:  Through the use of wheel spacers or wheels with
           non-standard offsets, the track width of the car may be increased
           over stock by .25" per side, front and rear.  This permitted track
           increase is separate from any track increased realized by installing
           permitted wider wheels, as long as such wheels have the
           standard Porsche offset.

      (e) Air Cleaner Element:  Any air cleaner element may be used.  The
           stock element housing must be retained.  This allows easier
           engine breathing without putting the engine at risk.

      (f) Mufflers:  Any muffler may be used, subject to site and
           instruction noise limitations.

      (g) CIS Components:  Early model CIS components may be replaced
           with corresponding later model components, except that the
           throttle base diameter may not be changed.

      (h) Solex:  All 356s are permitted Solex 40 P11 carburetors and
           corresponding intake manifolds.  For these carburetors only,
           jetting is free.

      (i) Chips/Rev Limiters/Ignition System:  Alternate DME computer
           chips may be used.  The stock rev limiter may be altered or
           substituted.  Electronic and transistor systems are permitted as
           long as the stock distributor is used.  The distributor may be
           recurved.  Bosch units that were standard for the engine may be
           substituted for Mirelli distributors.

      (j) Side Shifters:  914s may update to the late style side shift
           transmission linkage.

      (k) Tower Braces:  A front shock tower brace is permitted, limited to
           two mounting points on an existing part of the shock tower and
           a horizontal bar not more than 1.5" in diameter.

      (l) Turbo Tie Rod Ends:  911 turbo tie rods may be installed.

      (m) Adjustable Spring Plates:  Cars built before 1977 may install
           adjustable spring plates.  This provision for cars built before 1977
           recognizes that many such cars may be in need of replacement
           spring plates; for the competitive driver, the logical such choice
           may be the adjustable spring plates.  However, the newer cars
           are not likely to have worn out the spring plate bushings, and to
           allow them to change to the adjustable spring plates would tend
           to push all owners into making this somewhat expensive change
           in order to remain competitive.

      (n) 914 Rear Springs:  914's may run 140-lb. rear springs.  This
           allows the 914s to avoid buying a rear sway bar for the Improved
           Category which will likely be discarded if/when the car is
           prepared for Production Category.

      (o) Tire Types:  Any DOT-approved street tire may be used.  Racing
           tires are not permitted.  The Drivers Events Committee may
           designate any tire as a race tire.  Recapped tires are not allowed.

      (p) Tire Wear:  All tires must be DOT approved.  At all times,
           including after the last timed run, the tires must not show casing
           cord on the surface.

      (q) Tire & Wheel Sizes:  Appendix A shows the allowable sizes for
           tires and wheels.  In the Improved Category, drivers may include
           the '+' number.  Thus, if the listing shows 6 + 1, the driver may
           use a 7" wheel.  The upgrade in wheel width is permitted for this
           category as many drivers will want an extra set of wheels (one
           for street tires, one for sticky tires), and would prefer the wheels
           that offer the greatest performance.

      (r) Brake Cooling:  Brake cooling devices that attach to the spindle,
           but do not require more than 6" of tubing, are permitted.  This
           permits the CoolBrake approach, without getting into front
           spoilers and airflow hoses.  The increased cooling is appropriate
           for aggressive street use and a safety improvement for time
           trials.

      (s) Brake Bias Valves:  A brake bias valve may be installed as long as
           it does not provide for adjustment from the cockpit.

      (t) Batteries:  Cars delivered with two batteries may remove one of
           them.  The second battery is not really needed, and represents
           an extra maintenance expense when it must be replaced. 
           Alternate batteries may be used, to avoid the expense of the
           very large, late-model batteries, but they must be standard
           automotive batteries and they must be firmly mounted.  No
           motorcycle or mini batteries.

      (u) Camber:  Camber settings are limited to 2x at the front of rear-
           and mid-engined cars, 3x at the rear of rear- and mid-engined
           cars, 3x at the front of front-engined cars and 2x at the rear of
           front-engined cars.  Camber measurements shall be the average
           of the readings from both sides of the car, with the driver seated
           in the driver seat.  This is to compensate for the lack of a known
           perfectly level surface when measuring camber in the field.
           Limiting camber creates an even playing field for cars which may
           show variations from the factory in how much negative camber
           they can achieve through normal adjustments.

      (v) Thermal Reactors & Catalytic Converters:  Thermal reactors or
           catalytic converters may be replaced by a straight pipe, as long
           as no change is made to the headers.  This is to provide for
           longer engine life, as these components increase engine
           temperature and shorten engine life, especially under
           competition conditions.



4.3 PRODUCTION CATEGORY
      (a) Purpose:  The Production Category provides competition
           opportunity for drivers who want to get the most out of their
           Porsche, yet keep it reasonably streetable.  Relatively more
           expensive and non-reversable modifications are allowed,
           compared to the Improved Category.  Additionally, some
           modifications are permitted which trade increased power in
           performance for some decrease in engine reliability and
           longevity.  The changes are still limited, compared to the Super
           Street Category, but more to protect the integrity of the classes
           than for any other reason.  While the modifications allowed may
           result in a car that is somewhat streetable, and could be driven to
           the event, there is no requirement that the car have valid
           registration.

      (b) All modifications permitted in the Stock and Improved
           Categories are permitted.

      (c) Track Increase:  Through the use of wheel spacers or wheels with
           non-standard offsets, the track width of the car may be increased
           over stock by .5" per side, front and rear.  This is instead of, not
           in addition to, the increase permitted in the Improved Category. 
           This permitted track increase is separate from any track increased
           realized by installing permitted wider wheels, as long as such
           wheels have the standard Porsche offset.

      (d) Tails/Wings:  Rear spoiler leading edge must be attached to the
           car.  911/912 Porsches may run rear spoilers with dimensions
           equivalent to 911 stock Carrera or Turbo spoilers or smaller.  Rear
           vision must not be impaired.  Spoilers may not extend past the
           width of a factory stock-bodied the car.  A 914 may run a rear
           spoiler, not to exceed five (5) inches in height and not to exceed
           the width of the body.  Any 924 may run rear spoilers with
           dimensions equivalent to the 924 Turbo or 924 Carrera rear
           spoilers.  Any 928 may run a rear spoiler equivalent to a 928S
           rear spoiler.

      (e) Air Cleaner:  Any air cleaner element/housing may be used, or
           may be removed entirely.

      (f) Airflow:  Throttle bodies or venturis may be altered.  Airflow
           sensors may be altered or substituted.  Velocity stacks are
           permitted.  Jet sizes may be changed.  Turbo boost may be
           altered.  A different turbo unit and/or intercooler may be used,
           but multi-turbos are not permitted.

      (g) Flywheel:  A lightened flywheel/clutch/pressure plate assembly
           may be used.

      (h) Compression Ratio:  The compression ratio may be increased by
           .5 points.  This is a reasonable approach when rebuilding an
           engine.  Note that changing a 2.0 liter 4-cylinder to European
           pistons has the effect of raising compression by about .5 points;
           in such cases, no further compression increases are permitted.

      (i) Roller Cranks:  For 356s, any roller bearing crankshaft is
           permitted, provided the standard stroke is maintained.

      (j) Catalytic Converters/Thermal Reactors:  Catalytic converters and
           thermal reactors may be removed.  This is not allowed in the
           Improved Category, to support the streetability of those cars, but
           is appropriate for a car that is moving toward being primarily
           used for competition.  This also allows reasonable choices of
           exhaust header systems.

      (k) Exhaust Systems:  Alternate exhaust headers may be used. 
           Heaters may be removed.

      (l) Limited-Slip Differentials:  All cars may use any limited slip
           differential.

      (m) Airdams, Valance Panels:  An alternate airdam is permitted,
           provided that it does not extend past the forward edge of the
           bumper and does not extend to less than three (3) inches above
           the ground.  Replacement of the front valance panel/bumper and
           removal of the rear valance panel is permitted.

      (n) 356 Bumpers:  356s may remove bumpers.

      (o) Adjustable Spring Plates:  All cars may install adjustable spring
           plates.

      (p) Shocks:  Any shock absorber may be used.  

      (q) Plastic or Metal Bushings:  Plastic or metal bushing may be
           substituted for rubber.  This includes replacing shock-top rubber
           bushing with alternate materials.

      (r) Torsion Bars & Springs:  Alternate torsion bars and springs may
           be used.

      (t) Seats: Any seats may be used.  Two seats are required.

      (u) Brakes:  Brake cooling devices and systems which route air to
           the braking system are permitted.  914-4s may substitute calipers
           and rotors only from any 914.  The expense of changing the
           entire hub to upgrade 914 brakes is too severe.  914-6s may
           substitute calipers and rotors from any 911.  Calipers and rotors
           are free for all other Porsches.  For these cars, reasonable
           aftermarket brakes exist and are permitted in the interests of
           increased safety.

      (v) Battery Location:  Batteries may be relocated.

      (w) Fuel Cells:  Fuel cells may be used, but must be as close as
           possible to the same location as the original fuel tank.  In no case
           can the fuel cell be mounted closer to the center of the car than
           the original fuel tank.

      (x) Sway Bars:  All cars may use any sway bar.

      (y) Distributors:  Any distributor may be used.  Crankfire ignition is
           permitted.

      (z) Steering Wheels with Airbags:  Any steering wheel may be used,
           even if a steering wheel equipped with an airbag is removed.



4.4 SUPER-PRODUCTION CATEGORY
      (a)  Purpose:  This category is for cars that have been modified
           beyond the requirements of the Production Category only in very
           explicit ways.  Otherwise, all Production Category requirements
           are in effect.  This category provides a logical development
           pathway to Super Street.  Additionally, it provides a proper home
           for 3.2L conversions, as long as they are not modified beyond
           the limitations of the Production Category.

      (b) Class Bx:  For 4-cyliner, aircooled Porsches.  Maximum engine
           size is 2055cc.  Such a motor must be a legal, Production-
           Category motor.  Any DOT tire may be used.  Participants may
           choose either to: 

           ~ change to curburetors, or to

           ~ increase wheel width up to 8 inches.

      (c) Class Fx:  For all 6-cylinder, air-cooled engines, non-turbo. 
           Drivers may select either to 

           ~ upgrade tires and wheels (Any DOT tire may be used.  Wheels
           are free up to 8 inches in width.), or to 

           ~ run a non-original motor which would, in its original car, be a
           permissible motor in the Production Category, to a maximum of
           3.2 liters.


4.5 PRODIFIED CATEGORY
      (a) Due to the special capability of the 914 to provide race-car
           performance within very tight budget constraints, three Prodified
           classes are provided.

      (b) All modifications permitted to 914s in the Stock, Improved, and
           Production Categories are permitted.

      (c) Suspension modifications accomplished by machining or welding
           are permitted.

      (d) Drilling or grooving of brake rotors is permitted.  

      (e) Racing tires are permitted.  Tires that do not meet the size
           requirements of the Production Category, but which otherwise
           would be allowable in the Production Category, are permitted.

      (f) Rim widths are limited to 7" maximum.  Rim diameter is limited
           to 15" minimum.  Offset wheels are permitted.

      (g) Non standard gearing is permitted.

      (h) Float bowl baffling is permitted.

      (i) Compression ratio may be increased.

      (j) A track width increase up to 2" is permitted, along with wheel
           spacers and replacement wheel studs.

      (k) Locked differentials are permitted.

      (l) Any front air dam may be installed, provided it does not extend
           forward of the stock front bumper (excluding bumperettes), and
           does not extend rearward of the front wheel centerline.  Removal
           of the front valance panel/bumper and the rear valance is
           permitted.

      (m) Any rear aerodynamic device is permitted provided:
                 i.  It is within a 5-inch perimeter at the contour of a factory
                 stock car as viewed from above.
                 ii.  There is no forward-facing gap between the device and the
                 body of the car for the central 30 inches.
                 iii.  It does not extend closer than 6" to the ground.

      (n) Any brand pistons and cylinders may be used.  Overbore up to
           1.2 mm over stock is permitted.

      (o) Fiberglas fenders, hood, rear deck lid, engine cover, and rear
           bumpers may be substituted for the stock components.  Fiberglas
           doors are not permitted.



4.6 STREET MODIFIED CATEGORY
      (a) This is a category for highly modified cars that are still driven on
           the street.  Basically anything goes.  

      (b) Batteries:  Any battery may be used.

      (c) Tires:
           ~ Street tires: Any street tire/wheel combination may be used. 
           Tires must be DOT approved.

           ~ Race Tires:  Race tires may be used, but may not be mounted
           on wheels wider than seven (7) inches or one inch wider than
           stock, whichever is greater.  This leaves open the possibility of
           cars being competitive on very large street tires.

      (d) Interior:  The car must have full upholstery, carpeting and two
           seats.  This keeps the category separate from the Modified
           Category.

      (e) Fuel Tank Location:  Fuel tanks/cells may be relocated, but not
           into the passenger compartment.

      (f) Porsche:  The chassis, engine and transmission must be Porsche.

      (g) Glass:  The car must have full glass (no plexiglas windows).

      (h) Electrical:  Headlights, taillights, brake lights and turn signals
           must work.

      (i) Induction System:  Twin turbos may be used.  Fuel mixture may
           be any injection or carburetion system.  These changes are not
           permitted in the Production Category due to high costs.

      (j) Engine Parts:  Different cams may be used.  Any brand pistons
           and cylinders is permitted.  These changes are not permitted in
           the Production Category due to high costs.

      (k) Gears, Ring & Pinion:  Different gears and/or ring & pinion may
           be used.  These changes are not permitted in the Production
           Category due to high costs, and to maintain the integrity of the
           classes.

      (l) Tails, Wings, Airdams:  Any tail, wing or airdam is permitted. 
           The rear device may not obstruct rear vision.

      (m) Brake Bias Valves:  Any brake bias valve may be used.

      (n) Suspension Struts:  Any suspension strut may be used, except
           class Bs.

      (o) Camber:  Camber settings are free.

      (p) Welding/Machining:  Suspension modifications through welding
           or machining are permitted.



4.7 MODIFIED CATEGORY
      (a) Intention:  The Modified Category is intended for competition
           between production-model based cars.  Drivers of factory-built
           race cars are encouraged to enter them in the Exhibition
           Category.

      (b) Limitations:  Modified Category cars are those that exceed the
           limits permitted in the Super Street Category.  An original
           Porsche unibody (defined as: the rocker box section on both sides
           of the passenger compartment, the door posts for mounting the
           original door hinges, and the central tunnel through the
           passenger compartment.  These must remain in their original
           factory position.) is required and may be modified.  Bracing and
           supplemental stiffeners may be added.  Engine and transmission
           must be Porsche.  The original unibody suspension type and
           number of suspension pick-up points must be retained.  It is
           prohibited to attach multi-link front or rear suspension if not
           originally utilized.

      (c) Rollbars & Cages:  Full roll cages are required on time trial cars. 
           Roll bars and/or cages are recommended on autocross cars.



4.8 EXHIBITION CATEGORY
      (a) Exhibition Category is for cars that do not conform to any of the
           other categories or for drivers who want to enjoy running their
           cars without interefering with other drivers' efforts to earn points
           and awards.  (Drivers of Historic Porsches and of factory race cars
           are encouraged to participate in Exhibition Category).  There is a
           Class EX in which cars that participate are eligible for times and
           event trophies but not for year-end awards.

      (b) Exhibition cars are subject to all safety rules with allowance
           given for original equipment.  Original factory equipment not
           consistent with Porsche Club rules may be approved by the event
           chairman and chief tech inspector upon inspection of the car and
           equipment.



Three appendices, Appendix A:  Car Classes, Tires and Wheels, Appendix B:  
Summary of Classes, and Appendix C:  Summary of Modifications, could not be 
reduced from WordPerfect into straight ASCII text, without retyping them in 
their entirety.  It was not clear to the author that this effort was 
justified.  Further, it's not at all clear that the appendicies are going to 
fit very nicely into 80 columns, though it should be close.  This is all 
somewhat unfortunate, as the appendicies provide a very nice overview of the
classes and the rules.  

Contact *********** for mailed copies of these sections of the document.

Subject: I can't get my decklid open

Hi,
I need the advice of those of you out there w/ 914's.
My name is Brendin Harb and I'm new to the mailing list. I have
a 1972 914 and I can't get my front decklid open from inside the
passenger compartment. The problem is that the lever for the release
has a lock on it. I have the right key but the cylinder won't turn
the necessary 90 degrees to unlock itself. Has anyone else experienced
